## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of time (t) and current population (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where the growth rate depends on population size through various ecological mechanisms such as density dependence, Allee effects, and environmental carrying capacity.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Malthusian/exponential growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited exponential growth, growth rate proportional to population'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity K = 1/c1'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreases logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence exponent theta'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect (strong)', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Population has a minimum viable threshold below which it declines'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect (weak/multiplicative)', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**2 * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate increases more than linearly at low densities'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth model'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent birth rate with saturating resource competition'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent exponential growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate changes exponentially over time (e.g., environmental degradation)'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'General polynomial expansion of density-dependent effects'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Fractional power growth, sub- or super-linear dependence on population'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Cubic terms in P (e.g., P*(P-a)*(K-P)) → Allee effect with critical population threshold
- Product of P and (1 - P/K) → classic logistic density dependence with carrying capacity
- Logarithmic terms log(K/P) multiplied by P → Gompertz-type asymmetric growth near carrying capacity
- Negative quadratic term -c*P^2 alongside positive linear term c*P → self-limiting density-dependent mortality
- Growth rate independent of t (function of P only) → autonomous ODE indicating time-invariant environmental conditions
- Ratio of polynomials in P → saturating functional responses in birth or death rates
- dP/dt passing through zero at specific P values → equilibrium points (carrying capacity, extinction threshold)
- Sign change in dP/dt at intermediate P → bistability or Allee effect dynamics

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
$$0.7214(-1 + P/6.651)(1 - P/13.538)P + 0.7214(1 - P/13.538)P + 0.7214 P^{1/3}$$

Let me simplify. Let $a = 0.7214$, $b = 6.651$, $d = 13.538$.

First term: $a(-1 + P/b)(1 - P/d)P$
Second term: $a(1 - P/d)P$
Third term: $a P^{1/3}$

Combine first two terms: $a(1 - P/d)P[(-1 + P/b) + 1] = a(1 - P/d)P \cdot P/b = \frac{a}{b}P^2(1 - P/d)$

So GT = $\frac{a}{b}P^2 - \frac{a}{bd}P^3 + aP^{1/3}$

With numbers: $\frac{0.7214}{6.651}P^2 - \frac{0.7214}{6.651 \times 13.538}P^3 + 0.7214 P^{1/3}$

$$= 0.10846 P^2 - 0.008012 P^3 + 0.7214 P^{1/3}$$

So GT is: **$c_a P^3 + c_b P^2 + c_c P^{1/3}$** (a cubic in P plus a fractional power term, with no linear or constant terms).

The key basis functions are: $P^3$, $P^2$, and $P^{1/3}$.

Now I'll check each candidate. The critical question is whether each candidate can produce exactly $P^3 + P^2 + P^{1/3}$ (with appropriate coefficients) and nothing else.

**Key observations:**
- GT has NO constant term, NO linear P term, and NO $t$ dependence.
- GT requires $P^{1/3}$ — this is a fractional power that cannot be replicated by polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, sine/cosine, or rational functions of P.

Let me quickly categorize candidates by whether they can produce $P^{1/3}$:

Candidates with $P^{c}$ (free exponent): 14, 15, 17, 18, 27, 28, 30, 31, 37, 38, 39, 40, 42, 43, 44, 45, 47, 54, 55, 57, 59, 60, 62, 63, 68, 72, 75, 76, 77, 83, 87, 88, 89, 91, 93

Candidates with only integer powers, sin, cos, exp, log (no free exponent): These CANNOT match GT because they lack $P^{1/3}$.

Need $c_4 P^{c_3}\log(Pc_5+1) = c \cdot P^{1/3}$. But $P^{c_3}\log(Pc_5+1)$ cannot equal $P^{1/3}$ for all P (log is not a power function).

Candidate 28 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 29:

No $P^{1/3}$.

### Candidate 30:
$(Pc_0(P+c_1) + (P+c_2)(Pc_3+Pc_4(P+c_1)+P^{c_5}c_6(P+c_1)))/((P+c_1)(P+c_2))$

$= \frac{Pc_0}{P+c_2} + \frac{Pc_3}{(P+c_1)(P+c_2)} + Pc_4 + P^{c_5}c_6 + \frac{Pc_3}{...}$

Wait, let me expand more carefully.

Numerator: $Pc_0(P+c_1) + (P+c_2)[Pc_3 + Pc_4(P+c_1) + P^{c_5}c_6(P+c_1)]$

$= Pc_0(P+c_1) + (P+c_2)(P+c_1)[Pc_4 + P^{c_5}c_6] + (P+c_2)Pc_3$

Denominator: $(P+c_1)(P+c_2)$

$= \frac{Pc_0}{P+c_2} + Pc_4 + c_6 P^{c_5} + \frac{Pc_3}{P+c_1}$

Set $c_5 = 1/3$ to get $P^{1/3}$. But we also need $P^3$ and $P^2$. The remaining terms are $Pc_4$ (linear), $\frac{Pc_0}{P+c_2}$ (approaches constant for large P), $\frac{Pc_3}{P+c_1}$ (approaches constant). These cannot produce $P^3$ or $P^2$.

Candidate 30 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 31:
$(Pc_0((Pc_1)^{c_2}-1)(Pc_3+1) + Pc_4 + Pc_5(Pc_3+1) + c_6(Pc_3+1))/(Pc_3+1)$

$= Pc_0((Pc_1)^{c_2}-1) + \frac{Pc_4}{Pc_3+1} + Pc_5 + c_6$

$= c_0 c_1^{c_2} P^{1+c_2} - c_0 P + \frac{Pc_4}{Pc_3+1} + Pc_5 + c_6$

Set $c_2 = 1/3-1 = -2/3$: get $P^{1/3}$. But still need $P^3$ and $P^2$. The rational term $\frac{Pc_4}{Pc_3+1}$ approaches a constant. Cannot produce $P^3$ and $P^2$.

Candidate 31 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Need exp term to equal $P^{1/3}$. Impossible.

### Candidate 37:
$P^3c_0 + P^2c_1 + Pc_2((Pc_3)^{c_4}-1) + c_5$

$= P^3c_0 + P^2c_1 + c_2 c_3^{c_4} P^{1+c_4} - c_2 P + c_5$

Set $c_4 = 1/3 - 1 = -2/3$: $P^{1+(-2/3)} = P^{1/3}$. ✓

So: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + c_2 c_3^{-2/3} P^{1/3} - c_2 P + c_5$

GT = $-0.008012 P^3 + 0.10846 P^2 + 0.7214 P^{1/3}$ (no $P$ term, no constant)

Need $c_2 = 0$ (to kill $P$ term) and $c_5 = 0$ (to kill constant). But if $c_2 = 0$, then the $P^{1/3}$ term also vanishes! So we can't independently control $P$ and $P^{1/3}$.

Cannot match.

Candidate 37 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 38:
$Pc_0((Pc_1)^{c_2}-1) + Pc_3(P+c_4)(Pc_5+1) + c_6$

$= c_0 c_1^{c_2} P^{1+c_2} - c_0 P + c_3 c_5 P^3 + c_3(1+c_4 c_5)P^2 + c_3 c_4 P + c_6$

Set $c_2 = -2/3$: $P^{1/3}$ term. Need $P^3$, $P^2$ from the cubic part. Need linear terms to cancel: $-c_0 + c_3 c_4 = 0$, and $c_6 = 0$.

So: $c_0 c_1^{-2/3} P^{1/3} + c_3 c_5 P^3 + c_3(1+c_4 c_5)P^2 + (c_3 c_4 - c_0)P + c_6$

Set $c_3 c_4 = c_0$ and $c_6 = 0$. Then we have:
- $P^{1/3}$: $c_0 c_1^{-2/3}$ — free ✓
- $P^3$: $c_3 c_5$ — free ✓
- $P^2$: $c_3(1 + c_4 c_5)$ — free ✓
- $P$: 0 ✓
- constant: 0 ✓

This works! We have enough free parameters.

Let me verify: GT = $-0.008012 P^3 + 0.10846 P^2 + 0.7214 P^{1/3}$

We need:
- $c_3 c_5 = -0.008012$
- $c_3(1 + c_4 c_5) = 0.10846$
- $c_0 c_1^{-2/3} = 0.7214$
- $c_3 c_4 = c_0$
- $c_6 = 0$

6 unknowns ($c_0, c_1, c_2=-2/3, c_3, c_4, c_5$), 4 equations (excluding $c_2$ and $c_6$). This is solvable.

Candidate 38 verdict: [MATCH]

This works!
